<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Een_groep_gevangenen_zit_op_de_grond,_bewaakt_door_soldaten_voorbeeld_van_goe%E2%80%A6,_Bestanddeelnr_15865.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2658" data-file-width="2539" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Een_groep_gevangenen_zit_op_de_grond%2C_bewaakt_door_soldaten_voorbeeld_van_goe%E2%80%A6%2C_Bestanddeelnr_15865.jpg/210px-Een_groep_gevangenen_zit_op_de_grond%2C_bewaakt_door_soldaten_voorbeeld_van_goe%E2%80%A6%2C_Bestanddeelnr_15865.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Een_groep_gevangenen_zit_op_de_grond%2C_bewaakt_door_soldaten_voorbeeld_van_goe%E2%80%A6%2C_Bestanddeelnr_15865.jpg/315px-Een_groep_gevangenen_zit_op_de_grond%2C_bewaakt_door_soldaten_voorbeeld_van_goe%E2%80%A6%2C_Bestanddeelnr_15865.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Een_groep_gevangenen_zit_op_de_grond%2C_bewaakt_door_soldaten_voorbeeld_van_goe%E2%80%A6%2C_Bestanddeelnr_15865.jpg/420px-Een_groep_gevangenen_zit_op_de_grond%2C_bewaakt_door_soldaten_voorbeeld_van_goe%E2%80%A6%2C_Bestanddeelnr_15865.jpg 2x" width="210"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Een_groep_gevangenen_zit_op_de_grond,_bewaakt_door_soldaten_voorbeeld_van_goe%E2%80%A6,_Bestanddeelnr_15865.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dutch soldiers in the East Indies during the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Revolution" title="Indonesian National Revolution">Indonesian National Revolution</a>, 1946</div></div></div>
<p>The Netherlands, a small rich country in Western Europe, had spent centuries building up its empire. By 1940 it consisted mostly of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a> (now Indonesia). Its massive oil reserves provided about 14 percent of the Dutch national product and supported a large population of ethnic Dutch government officials and businessmen in Jakarta and other major cities. The Netherlands was overrun and almost starved to death by the Nazis during the war, and Japan sank the Dutch fleet in seizing the East Indies. In 1945 the Netherlands could not regain these islands on its own; it did so by depending on British military help and American financial grants. By the time Dutch soldiers returned, an independent government under <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">Sukarno</a>, originally set up by the Japanese, was in power. The Dutch in the East Indies, and at home, were practically unanimous (except for the Communists) that Dutch power and prestige and wealth depended on an extremely expensive war to regain the islands. Compromises were negotiated, were trusted by neither side. When the Indonesian Republic successfully suppressed a large-scale communist revolt, the United States realized that it needed the nationalist government as an ally in the Cold War. Dutch possession was an obstacle to American Cold War goals, so Washington forced the Dutch to grant full independence. A few years later, Sukarno seized all Dutch properties and expelled all <a href="/wiki/Indo_people" title="Indo people">ethnic Dutch</a>—over 300,000—as well as several hundred thousand ethnic Indonesians who supported the Dutch cause. In the aftermath, the Netherlands prospered greatly in the 1950s and 1960s but nevertheless public opinion was bitterly hostile to the United States for betrayal. Washington remained baffled why the Dutch were so inexplicably enamored of an obviously hopeless cause.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The Netherlands also had one other major colony, Dutch Guiana in South America, which became independent as <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> in 1975.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Nations_Trust_Territories">United Nations Trust Territories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: United Nations Trust Territories">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Trust_Territories" title="United Nations Trust Territories">United Nations Trust Territories</a></div>
<p>When the United Nations was formed in 1945, it established trust territories. These territories included the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">League of Nations mandate</a> territories which had not achieved independence by 1945, along with the former <a href="/wiki/Italian_Somaliland" title="Italian Somaliland">Italian Somaliland</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Trust_Territory_of_the_Pacific_Islands" title="Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands">Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands</a> was transferred from Japanese to US administration. By 1990 all but one of the trust territories had achieved independence, either as independent states or by merger with another independent state; the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Northern Mariana Islands">Northern Mariana Islands</a> elected to become a commonwealth of the United States.
</p>
<h4><span id="The_emergence_of_the_Third_World_.281945.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_emergence_of_the_Third_World_(1945–present)">The emergence of the Third World (1945–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: The emergence of the Third World (1945–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Africa_cs_poster.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="325" data-file-width="239" decoding="async" height="272" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/85/Africa_cs_poster.jpg/200px-Africa_cs_poster.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/85/Africa_cs_poster.jpg 1.5x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Africa_cs_poster.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Czechoslovak anti-colonialist propaganda poster: "Africa – in fight for freedom".</div></div></div>
<p>Newly independent states organised themselves in order to oppose continued economic colonialism by former imperial powers. The <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> constituted itself around the main figures of <a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru" title="Jawaharlal Nehru">Jawaharlal Nehru</a>, the first Prime Minister of India, <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">Sukarno</a>, the Indonesian president, <a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">Josip Broz Tito</a> the Communist leader of <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser" title="Gamal Abdel Nasser">Gamal Abdel Nasser</a>, head of Egypt. In 1955 these leaders gathered at the <a href="/wiki/Bandung_Conference" title="Bandung Conference">Bandung Conference</a> along with <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">Sukarno</a>, the leader of Indonesia, and <a href="/wiki/Zhou_Enlai" title="Zhou Enlai">Zhou Enlai</a>, Premier of the People's Republic of China. In 1960, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_General_Assembly" title="UN General Assembly">UN General Assembly</a> voted the <a href="/wiki/Declaration_on_the_Granting_of_Independence_to_Colonial_Countries_and_Peoples" title="Declaration on the Granting of Independence to Colonial Countries and Peoples">Declaration on the Granting of Independence to Colonial Countries and Peoples</a>. The next year, the Non-Aligned Movement was officially created in <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> (1961), and was followed in 1964 by the creation of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Conference_on_Trade_and_Development" title="United Nations Conference on Trade and Development">United Nations Conference on Trade and Development</a> (UNCTAD) which tried to promote a <a href="/wiki/New_International_Economic_Order" title="New International Economic Order">New International Economic Order</a> (NIEO). The NIEO was opposed to the 1944 <a href="/wiki/Bretton_Woods_system" title="Bretton Woods system">Bretton Woods system</a>, which had benefited the leading states which had created it, and remained in force until 1971 after the United States' suspension of convertibility from dollars to gold. The main tenets of the NIEO were:
</p>
<ol><li>Developing countries must be entitled to regulate and control the activities of <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational corporations</a> operating within their territory.</li>
<li>They must be free to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nationalise" title="Nationalise">nationalise</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Expropriate" title="Expropriate">expropriate</a> foreign property on conditions favourable to them.</li>
<li>They must be free to set up associations of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_commodities" title="Primary commodities">primary commodities</a> producers similar to the <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">Organisation of the Petroleum Exporting Countries</a>, created on September 14, 1960, to protest pressure by major oil companies (mostly owned by U.S., British, and Dutch nationals) to reduce oil prices and payments to producers); all other states must recognise this right and refrain from taking economic, military, or political measures calculated to restrict it.</li>
<li>International trade should be based on the need to ensure stable, equitable, and remunerative prices for raw materials, generalised non-reciprocal and non-discriminatory tariff preferences, as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transfer_of_technology" title="Transfer of technology">transfer of technology</a> to developing countries; and should provide economic and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Technical_assistance" title="Technical assistance">technical assistance</a> without any <a href="/wiki/Conditionality" title="Conditionality">strings attached</a>.</li></ol>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Countries_by_Human_Development_Index_(2020).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3087" data-file-width="6915" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Countries_by_Human_Development_Index_%282020%29.png/350px-Countries_by_Human_Development_Index_%282020%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Countries_by_Human_Development_Index_%282020%29.png/525px-Countries_by_Human_Development_Index_%282020%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Countries_by_Human_Development_Index_%282020%29.png/700px-Countries_by_Human_Development_Index_%282020%29.png 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Countries_by_Human_Development_Index_(2020).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Human_Development_Index" title="UN Human Development Index">UN Human Development Index</a> (HDI) is a quantitative index of development, an alternative to the classic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gross_Domestic_Product" title="Gross Domestic Product">Gross Domestic Product</a> (GDP), which some use as a proxy to define the <a href="/wiki/Third_World" title="Third World">Third World</a>. While the GDP only calculates economic wealth, the HDI includes <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public health</a> and <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> as fundamental factors of a good <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">quality of life</a>. Countries in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cone" title="Southern Cone">Southern Cone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a> generally have better standards of living than countries in <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">East Africa</a>, parts of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The UNCTAD however wasn't very effective in implementing the NIEO, and social and economic inequalities between industrialized countries and the Third World grew throughout the 1960s until the 21st century. The <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">1973 oil crisis</a> which followed the <a href="/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War" title="Yom Kippur War">Yom Kippur War</a> (October 1973) was triggered by the OPEC which decided an embargo against the US and Western countries, causing a fourfold increase in the price of oil, which lasted five months, starting on October 17, 1973, and ending on March 18, 1974. OPEC nations then agreed, on January 7, 1975, to raise crude oil prices by 10%. At that time, OPEC nations – including many who had recently nationalized their oil industries – joined the call for a New International Economic Order to be initiated by coalitions of primary producers. Concluding the First OPEC Summit in Algiers they called for stable and just commodity prices, an international food and agriculture program, technology transfer from North to South, and the democratization of the economic system. But industrialized countries quickly began to look for substitutes to OPEC petroleum, with the oil companies investing the majority of their research capital in the US and European countries or others, politically sure countries. The OPEC lost more and more influence on the world prices of oil.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1979_energy_crisis" title="1979 energy crisis">second oil crisis</a> occurred in the wake of the 1979 <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Revolution" title="Iranian Revolution">Iranian Revolution</a>. Then, the 1982 <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_debt_crisis" title="Latin American debt crisis">Latin American debt crisis</a> exploded in Mexico first, then Argentina and Brazil, which proved unable to pay back their debts, jeopardizing the existence of the international economic system.
</p><p>The 1990s were characterized by the prevalence of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_consensus" title="Washington consensus">Washington consensus</a> on <a href="/wiki/Neoliberalism" title="Neoliberalism">neoliberal</a> policies, "<a href="/wiki/Structural_adjustment" title="Structural adjustment">structural adjustment</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Shock_therapy_(economics)" title="Shock therapy (economics)">shock therapies</a>" for the former Communist states.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Decolonization_of_Africa">Decolonization of Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Decolonization of Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decolonization_of_Africa" title="Decolonization of Africa">Decolonization of Africa</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png/220px-British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png/330px-British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png/440px-British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:British_Decolonisation_in_Africa.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British decolonisation in Africa</div></div></div>
<p>The decolonization of North Africa, and sub-Saharan Africa took place in the mid-to-late 1950s, very suddenly, with little preparation. There was widespread unrest and organized revolts, especially in French Algeria, Portuguese Angola, the Belgian Congo and British Kenya.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1945, Africa had four independent countries – Egypt, Ethiopia, Liberia, and South Africa.
</p><p>After Italy's defeat in World War II, France and the UK occupied the former Italian colonies. <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a> became an independent kingdom in 1951. <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a> was merged with Ethiopia in 1952. Italian Somaliland was governed by the UK, and by Italy after 1954, until its independence in 1960.
</p><p>By 1977 European colonial rule in mainland Africa had ended. Most of Africa's island countries had also become independent, although <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="Réunion">Réunion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a> remain part of France. However the black majorities in <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia" title="Rhodesia">Rhodesia</a> and South Africa were disenfranchised until 1979 in <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia" title="Rhodesia">Rhodesia</a>, which became <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zimbabwe-Rhodesia" title="Zimbabwe-Rhodesia">Zimbabwe-Rhodesia</a> that year and Zimbabwe the next, and until 1994 in South Africa. <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a>, Africa's last UN Trust Territory, became independent of South Africa in 1990.
</p><p>Most independent African countries exist within prior colonial borders. However <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> merged <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Morocco" title="French Morocco">French Morocco</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Morocco" title="Spanish Morocco">Spanish Morocco</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> formed from the merger of <a href="/wiki/British_Somaliland" title="British Somaliland">British Somaliland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_Somaliland" title="Italian Somaliland">Italian Somaliland</a>. Eritrea merged with Ethiopia in 1952, but became an independent country in 1993.
</p><p>Most African countries became independent as <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republics</a>. <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Eswatini" title="Eswatini">Eswatini</a> remain monarchies under dynasties that predate colonial rule. <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a> gained independence as monarchies, but all four countries' monarchs were later deposed, and they became republics.
</p><p>African countries cooperate in various multi-state associations. The <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> includes all 55 African states. There are several regional associations of states, including the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a>, some of which have overlapping membership.
</p>
<ul><li><span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="United Kingdom"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a></span>: <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> (1956); <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a> (1957); <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> (1960); <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tanganyika_(1961%E2%80%931964)" title="Tanganyika (1961–1964)">Tanganyika</a> (1961); <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> (1962); <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Zanzibar" title="Sultanate of Zanzibar">Sultanate of Zanzibar</a> (1963); <a href="/wiki/Malawi" title="Malawi">Malawi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> (1964); <a href="/wiki/The_Gambia" title="The Gambia">Gambia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia" title="Rhodesia">Rhodesia</a> (1965); <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a> (1966); <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swaziland" title="Swaziland">Swaziland</a> (1968); <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a> (1976)</li>
<li><span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="France"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a></span>: <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a> (1956); <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a> (1958); <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Togo" title="Togo">Togo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benin" title="Benin">Benin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">Burkina Faso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a> (1960); <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> (1962); <a href="/wiki/Comoros" title="Comoros">Comoros</a> (1975); <a href="/wiki/Djibouti" title="Djibouti">Djibouti</a> (1977)</li>
<li><span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="Spain"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="750" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/23px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/35px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/45px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a></span>: <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a> (1968)</li>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Decolonization_in_the_Americas_after_1945">Decolonization in the Americas after 1945</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Decolonization in the Americas after 1945">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Decolonization_of_the_Americas" title="Decolonization of the Americas">Decolonization of the Americas</a></div>
<ul><li><span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="United Kingdom"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a></span>: <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Newfoundland" title="Dominion of Newfoundland">Newfoundland</a> (formerly an independent dominion but under direct British rule since 1934) (1949, union with Canada); <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a> (1962); <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a> (1966); <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a> (1973); <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a> (1974); <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a> (1976, removal of Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> as head of state, transition to republic); <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a> (1978); <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="St. Vincent and the Grenadines">St. Vincent and the Grenadines</a> (1979); <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a> (1981); <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis">Saint Kitts and Nevis</a> (1983); <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> (2021, removal of Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> as head of state, transition to republic).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="Netherlands"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a></span>: <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">Netherlands Antilles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> (1954, both becoming constituent countries of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a>), 1975 (independence of Suriname)</li>
<li><span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="Denmark"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" data-file-height="560" data-file-width="1070" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Flag_of_Denmark_%28state%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Denmark_%28state%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Flag_of_Denmark_%28state%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Denmark_%28state%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Flag_of_Denmark_%28state%29.svg/46px-Flag_of_Denmark_%28state%29.svg.png 2x" title="no" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Danish_Realm" title="Danish Realm">Denmark</a></span>: <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> (1979, became an autonomous territory of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Denmark" title="Kingdom of Denmark">Kingdom of Denmark</a>).</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Decolonization_of_Asia">Decolonization of Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Decolonization of Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Decolonization_of_Asia" title="Decolonization of Asia">Decolonization of Asia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Colonization_1945.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="638" data-file-width="1438" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Colonization_1945.png/330px-Colonization_1945.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Colonization_1945.png/495px-Colonization_1945.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Colonization_1945.png/660px-Colonization_1945.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Colonization_1945.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Western European colonial empires in Asia and Africa all collapsed in the years after 1945</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Partition_of_India.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="450" decoding="async" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Partition_of_India.PNG/220px-Partition_of_India.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Partition_of_India.PNG/330px-Partition_of_India.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Partition_of_India.PNG/440px-Partition_of_India.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Partition_of_India.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Four nations (<a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Ceylon" title="Dominion of Ceylon">Dominion of Ceylon</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_of_Burma" title="Union of Burma">Union of Burma</a>) that gained independence in 1947 and 1948</div></div></div>
<p>Japan expanded its occupation of Chinese territory during the 1930s, and occupied <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> during World War II. After the war, the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_colonial_empire" title="Japanese colonial empire">Japanese colonial empire</a> was dissolved, and national independence movements resisted the re-imposition of colonial control by European countries and the United States.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%931949)" title="Republic of China (1912–1949)">Republic of China</a> regained control of Japanese-occupied territories in Manchuria and eastern China, as well as Taiwan. Only Hong Kong and Macau remained in outside control.
</p><p>The Allied powers divided Korea into two occupation zones, which became the states of <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> became independent of the US in 1946.
</p><p>The Netherlands recognized <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>'s independence in 1949, after a four-year <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Revolution" title="Indonesian National Revolution">independence struggle</a>. Indonesia annexed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Netherlands_New_Guinea" title="Netherlands New Guinea">Netherlands New Guinea</a> in 1963, and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Timor" title="Portuguese Timor">Portuguese Timor</a> in 1975. In 2002, former Portuguese Timor became independent as <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a>.
</p><p>The following list shows the colonial powers following the end of hostilities in 1945, and their colonial or administrative possessions. The year of decolonization is given chronologically in parentheses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="United Kingdom"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a></span>: <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Transjordan" title="Emirate of Transjordan">Transjordan</a> (1946), <a href="/wiki/Presidencies_and_provinces_of_British_India" title="Presidencies and provinces of British India">British India</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> (1947); <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">British Mandate of Palestine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Burma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Ceylon</a> (1948); <a href="/wiki/British_Malaya" title="British Malaya">British Malaya</a> (1957); <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a> (1961); <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sarawak" title="Kingdom of Sarawak">Kingdom of Sarawak</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Borneo" title="North Borneo">North Borneo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> (1963); <a href="/wiki/Maldives" title="Maldives">Maldives</a> (1965); <a href="/wiki/Southern_Movement" title="Southern Movement">Aden</a> (1967); <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> (1971); <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a> (1984); <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> (1997)</li>
<li><span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="France"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a></span>: <a href="/wiki/French_India" title="French India">French India</a> (1954) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indochina" title="Indochina">Indochina</a> comprising <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> (1945), <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a> (1953) and <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a> (1953)</li>
<li><span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="Portugal"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Portugal.svg/23px-Flag_of_Portugal.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Portugal.svg/35px-Flag_of_Portugal.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Portugal.svg/45px-Flag_of_Portugal.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a></span>: <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India" title="Portuguese India">Portuguese India</a> (1961); <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a> (1975); <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> (1999)</li>
<li><span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="United States"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a></span>: <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> (1946)</li>
<li><span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="Netherlands"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a></span>: <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> (1949)</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Decolonization_in_Europe">Decolonization in Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Decolonization in Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nyet,_nyet,_Soviet_(11).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3864" data-file-width="5152" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Nyet%2C_nyet%2C_Soviet_%2811%29.jpg/220px-Nyet%2C_nyet%2C_Soviet_%2811%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Nyet%2C_nyet%2C_Soviet_%2811%29.jpg/330px-Nyet%2C_nyet%2C_Soviet_%2811%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Nyet%2C_nyet%2C_Soviet_%2811%29.jpg/440px-Nyet%2C_nyet%2C_Soviet_%2811%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nyet,_nyet,_Soviet_(11).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A protest sign from the second half of the 20th century calling on U.N. to abolish <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_colonialism" title="Soviet colonialism">Soviet colonialism</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic states</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Italy had occupied the <a href="/wiki/Dodecanese" title="Dodecanese">Dodecanese</a> islands in 1912, but Italian occupation ended after World War II, and the islands were integrated into Greece. British rule ended in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Cyprus_(1878%E2%80%931960)" title="British Cyprus (1878–1960)">Cyprus</a> in 1960, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Malta#Malta_in_the_British_Empire_(1800–1964)" title="History of Malta">Malta</a> in 1964, and both islands became independent republics.
</p><p>Soviet control of its non-Russian member republics weakened as movements for democratization and self-government gained strength during the late 1980s, and four republics declared independence in 1990 and 1991. The <a href="/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1991 Soviet coup d'état attempt">Soviet coup d'état attempt</a> in August 1991 accelerated the breakup of the USSR, which formally ended on December 26, 1991. The <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Republics of the Soviet Union">Republics of the Soviet Union</a> become sovereign states—<a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a> (formerly called Byelorussia,) <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>. Historian Robert Daniels says, "A special dimension that the anti-Communist revolutions shared with some of their predecessors was decolonization."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Moscow's policy had long been to settle ethnic Russians in the non-Russian republics. After independence, minority rights has been an issue for Russian-speakers in some republics and for <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Russia" title="Languages of Russia">non-Russian-speakers</a> in Russia; see <a href="/wiki/Russians_in_the_Baltic_states" title="Russians in the Baltic states">Russians in the Baltic states</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the Russian Federation continues to apply political, economic, and military pressure on former Soviet colonies. In 2014, it <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">annexed Ukraine's Crimean peninsula</a>, the first and only such action in Europe since the end of the Second World War.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Decolonization_of_Oceania">Decolonization of Oceania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Decolonization of Oceania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The decolonization of Oceania occurred after World War II when nations in Oceania achieved independence by transitioning from European colonial rule to full independence.
</p>
<ul><li><span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="United Kingdom"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a></span>: <a href="/wiki/Tonga" title="Tonga">Tonga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a> (1970); <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a> (1978); <a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">Kiribati</a> (1979)</li>
<li><span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="United Kingdom"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a></span> and <span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="France"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a></span>: <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a> (1980)</li>
<li><span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="Australia"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg/46px-Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a></span>: <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a> (1968); <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> (1975)</li>
<li><span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="New Zealand"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg/23px-Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg/35px-Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg/46px-Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a></span>: <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">Samoa</a> (1962)</li>
<li><span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="United States"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a></span>: <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia" title="Federated States of Micronesia">Federated States of Micronesia</a> (1986); <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a> (1994)</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Challenges">Challenges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Challenges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Typical challenges of decolonization include <a href="/wiki/State-building" title="State-building">state-building</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nation-building" title="Nation-building">nation-building</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Economic_development" title="Economic development">economic development</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State-building">State-building</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: State-building">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/State-building" title="State-building">State-building</a></div>
<p>After independence, the new states needed to establish or strengthen the institutions of a sovereign state – governments, laws, a military, schools, administrative systems, and so on. The amount of self-rule granted prior to independence, and assistance from the colonial power and/or international organizations after independence, varied greatly between colonial powers, and between individual colonies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Glassner,_Martin_Ira_1980_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Glassner,_Martin_Ira_1980-55">[55]</a></sup>
</p><p>Except for a few absolute monarchies, most post-colonial states are either <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republics</a> or <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchies</a>. These new states had to devise <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">constitutions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electoral_system" title="Electoral system">electoral systems</a>, and other institutions of <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language_policy">Language policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Language policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From the perspective of <a href="/wiki/Language_policy" title="Language policy">language policy</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Language_politics" title="Language politics">language politics</a>), "linguistic decolonization" entails the replacement of a colonizing (imperial) power's language with a given colony's indigenous language in the function of <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a>. With the exception of colonies in <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a>, linguistic decolonization did not take place in the former colonies-turned-independent states on the other continents ("Rest of the World").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The persistent absence of linguistic decolonization is known as <a href="/wiki/Linguistic_imperialism" title="Linguistic imperialism">linguistic imperialism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nation-building">Nation-building</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Nation-building">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nation-building" title="Nation-building">Nation-building</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Black_Star_Monument,_Accra,_Ghana.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1201" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Black_Star_Monument%2C_Accra%2C_Ghana.JPG/220px-Black_Star_Monument%2C_Accra%2C_Ghana.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Black_Star_Monument%2C_Accra%2C_Ghana.JPG/330px-Black_Star_Monument%2C_Accra%2C_Ghana.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Black_Star_Monument%2C_Accra%2C_Ghana.JPG/440px-Black_Star_Monument%2C_Accra%2C_Ghana.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Black_Star_Monument,_Accra,_Ghana.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><center>The <b>Black Star Monument</b> in <a href="/wiki/Accra" title="Accra">Accra</a>, built by <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>'s first president <a href="/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah" title="Kwame Nkrumah">Kwame Nkrumah</a> to commemorate the country's independence</center></div></div></div>
<p>Nation-building is the process of creating a sense of identification with, and loyalty to, the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Nation-building projects seek to replace loyalty to the old colonial power, and/or tribal or regional loyalties, with loyalty to the new state. Elements of nation-building include creating and promoting symbols of the state like a flag, a coat of arms and an anthem, monuments, official histories, national sports teams, codifying one or more Indigenous <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official languages</a>, and replacing colonial place-names with local ones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Glassner,_Martin_Ira_1980_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-Glassner,_Martin_Ira_1980-55">[55]</a></sup> Nation-building after independence often continues the work began by independence movements during the colonial period.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Settled_populations">Settled populations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Settled populations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Settler_colonialism" title="Settler colonialism">Settler colonialism</a></div>
<p>Decolonization is not an easy matter in colonies with large settler populations, particularly if they have been there for several generations. When settlers remain in former colonies after independence, colonialism is ongoing and takes the form of <a href="/wiki/Settler_colonialism" title="Settler colonialism">settler colonialism</a>, which is highly resistant to decolonisation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup>
</p><p>In a few cases, settler populations have been <a href="/wiki/Repatriation" title="Repatriation">repatriated</a>. For instance, the decolonization of <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> by France was particularly uneasy due to the large European population (see also <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pied_noir" title="Pied noir">pied noir</a></i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cook_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cook-61">[61]</a></sup> which largely evacuated to France when Algeria became independent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ladepeche_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-ladepeche-62">[62]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia" title="Rhodesia">Rhodesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Mugabe" title="Robert Mugabe">Robert Mugabe</a> seized property from white African farmers, killing several of them, and forcing the survivors to emigrate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cybriwsky_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cybriwsky-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> A large Indian community lived in <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> as a result of Britain colonizing both India and East Africa, and <a href="/wiki/Idi_Amin" title="Idi Amin">Idi Amin</a> <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_Asians_from_Uganda" title="Expulsion of Asians from Uganda">expelled them</a> for domestic political gain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Drive_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Drive-65">[65]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_development">Economic development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Economic development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economic_development" title="Economic development">Economic development</a></div>
<p>Newly independent states also had to develop independent economic institutions – a national currency, banks, companies, regulation, tax systems, etc.
</p><p>Many colonies were serving as resource colonies which produced raw materials and agricultural products, and as a captive market for goods manufactured in the colonizing country. Many decolonized countries created programs to promote <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrialization" title="Industrialization">industrialization</a>. Some nationalized industries and infrastructure, and some engaged in <a href="/wiki/Land_reform" title="Land reform">land reform</a> to redistribute land to individual farmers or create collective farms.
</p><p>Some decolonized countries maintain strong economic ties with the former colonial power. The <a href="/wiki/CFA_franc" title="CFA franc">CFA franc</a> is a currency shared by 14 countries in West and Central Africa, mostly former French colonies. The CFA franc is guaranteed by the French treasury.
</p><p>After independence, many countries created regional economic associations to promote trade and economic development among neighboring countries, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">Association of Southeast Asian Nations</a> (ASEAN), the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a> (ECOWAS), and the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council" title="Gulf Cooperation Council">Gulf Cooperation Council</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_on_the_colonizers">Effects on the colonizers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Effects on the colonizers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/John_Kenneth_Galbraith" title="John Kenneth Galbraith">John Kenneth Galbraith</a> argues that the post–World War II decolonization was brought about for economic reasons. In <i>A Journey Through Economic Time</i>, he writes: </p><blockquote><p>"The engine of economic well-being was now within and between the advanced industrial countries. Domestic <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">economic growth</a> – as now measured and much discussed – came to be seen as far more important than the erstwhile colonial trade.... The economic effect in the United States from the granting of independence to the Philippines was unnoticeable, partly due to the <a href="/wiki/Bell_Trade_Act" title="Bell Trade Act">Bell Trade Act</a>, which allowed American monopoly in the economy of the Philippines. The departure of India and Pakistan made small economic difference in the United Kingdom. <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> economists calculated that the economic effect from the loss of the great Dutch empire in Indonesia was compensated for by a couple of years or so of domestic post-war economic growth. The end of the colonial era is celebrated in the history books as a triumph of national aspiration in the former colonies and of benign good sense on the part of the colonial powers. Lurking beneath, as so often happens, was a strong current of economic interest – or in this case, disinterest."</p></blockquote>
<p>In general, the release of the colonized caused little economic loss to the colonizers. Part of the reason for this was that major costs were eliminated while major benefits were obtained by alternate means. Decolonization allowed the colonizer to disclaim responsibility for the colonized. The colonizer no longer had the burden of obligation, financial or otherwise, to their colony. However, the colonizer continued to be able to obtain cheap goods and labor as well as economic benefits (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suez_Canal_Crisis" title="Suez Canal Crisis">Suez Canal Crisis</a>) from the former colonies. Financial, political and military pressure could still be used to achieve goals desired by the colonizer. Thus decolonization allowed the goals of colonization to be largely achieved, but without its burdens.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural">Cultural</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Cultural">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Kenyan writer <a href="/wiki/Ng%C5%A9g%C4%A9_wa_Thiong%27o" title="Ngũgĩ wa Thiong'o">Ngũgĩ wa Thiong'o</a> has written about colonization and decolonization in the film universe. Born in Ethiopia, filmmaker <a href="/wiki/Haile_Gerima" title="Haile Gerima">Haile Gerima</a> describes the "colonization of the unconscious" he describes experiencing as a child:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kato2007_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-kato2007-66">[66]</a></sup>
</p>
<blockquote><p>...as kids, we tried to act out the things we had seen in the movies. We used to play cowbows and Indians in the mountains around Gondar...We acted out the roles of these heroes, identifying with the cowboys conquering the Indians. We didn't identify with the Indians at all and we never wanted the Indians to win. Even in Tarzan movies, we would become totally galvanized by the activities of the hero and follow the story from his point of view, completely caught up in the structure of the story. Whenever Africans sneaked up behind Tarzan, we would scream our heads off, trying to warn him that 'they' were coming".</p></blockquote>
<p>In Asia, <a href="/wiki/Kung_fu_film" title="Kung fu film">kung fu cinema</a> emerged at a time Japan wanted to reach Asian populations in other countries by way of its cultural influence. The surge in popularity of kung fu movies began in the late 1960s through the 1970s. Local populations were depicted as protagonists opposing "imperialists" (foreigners) and their "Chinese collaborators".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kato2007_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-kato2007-66">[66]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Assassinated_anti-colonialist_leaders">Assassinated anti-colonialist leaders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Assassinated anti-colonialist leaders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gandhi_with_Lord_and_Lady_Mountbatten_1947.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="370" data-file-width="537" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Gandhi_with_Lord_and_Lady_Mountbatten_1947.jpg/220px-Gandhi_with_Lord_and_Lady_Mountbatten_1947.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Gandhi_with_Lord_and_Lady_Mountbatten_1947.jpg/330px-Gandhi_with_Lord_and_Lady_Mountbatten_1947.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Gandhi_with_Lord_and_Lady_Mountbatten_1947.jpg/440px-Gandhi_with_Lord_and_Lady_Mountbatten_1947.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gandhi_with_Lord_and_Lady_Mountbatten_1947.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gandhi in 1947, with Lord <a href="/wiki/Louis_Mountbatten,_1st_Earl_Mountbatten_of_Burma" title="Louis Mountbatten, 1st Earl Mountbatten of Burma">Louis Mountbatten</a>, Britain's last Viceroy of India, and his wife Vicereine <a href="/wiki/Edwina_Mountbatten,_Countess_Mountbatten_of_Burma" title="Edwina Mountbatten, Countess Mountbatten of Burma">Edwina Mountbatten</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="424" data-file-width="467" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg/220px-Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg/330px-Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg/440px-Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Patrice_Lumumba_official_portrait.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Patrice_Lumumba" title="Patrice Lumumba">Patrice Lumumba</a>, first democratically elected <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Prime Minister of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Prime Minister</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville)">Congo-Léopoldville</a>, was murdered by Belgian-supported <a href="/wiki/State_of_Katanga" title="State of Katanga">Katangan separatists</a> in 1961.</div></div></div>
<p>A <i>non-exhaustive</i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_assassinated_people" title="List of assassinated people">list of assassinated leaders</a> would include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Tiradentes" title="Tiradentes">Tiradentes</a> was a leading member of the Brazilian seditious movement known as the <a href="/wiki/Inconfid%C3%AAncia_Mineira" title="Inconfidência Mineira">Inconfidência Mineira</a>, against the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a>. He fought for an independent Brazilian republic.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi" title="Mahatma Gandhi">Mohandas Karamchand Gandhi</a>, nonviolent leader of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">Indian independence movement</a> was assassinated in 1948 by <a href="/wiki/Nathuram_Godse" title="Nathuram Godse">Nathuram Godse</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ruben_Um_Nyob%C3%A9" title="Ruben Um Nyobé">Ruben Um Nyobé</a>, leader of the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_the_Peoples_of_Cameroon" title="Union of the Peoples of Cameroon">Union of the Peoples of Cameroon</a> (UPC), was killed by the French Army in the rain forest where he was hiding, near his native village, Boumnyebel, being shot several times, falling on the edge of a tree trunk which he was trying to step over; it was in the department of Nyong-et-Kéllé in an area occupied by the Bassa ethnic group of which he was also a native.  <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> His body was then mutilated and buried in an unmarked grave.  <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Barth%C3%A9lemy_Boganda" title="Barthélemy Boganda">Barthélemy Boganda</a>, leader of a nationalist <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> movement, who died in a plane-crash on March 29, 1959, eight days before the last elections of the colonial era. The French SDECE or his wife are the main suspects.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix-Roland_Moumi%C3%A9" title="Félix-Roland Moumié">Félix-Roland Moumié</a>, successor to Ruben Um Nyobe at the head of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cameroon%27s_People_Union" title="Cameroon's People Union">Cameroon's People Union</a>, assassinated in <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a> in 1960 by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SDECE" title="SDECE">SDECE</a> (French secret services).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Patrice_Lumumba" title="Patrice Lumumba">Patrice Lumumba</a>, the first Prime Minister of the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, was assassinated on January 17, 1961.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a> nationalist <a href="/wiki/Louis_Rwagasore" title="Louis Rwagasore">Louis Rwagasore</a> was assassinated on October 13, 1961, while <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Ngendandumwe" title="Pierre Ngendandumwe">Pierre Ngendandumwe</a>, Burundi's first <a href="/wiki/Hutu" title="Hutu">Hutu</a> prime minister, was also murdered on January 15, 1965.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sylvanus_Olympio" title="Sylvanus Olympio">Sylvanus Olympio</a>, the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Togo" title="List of Presidents of Togo">president of Togo</a>, was assassinated on January 13, 1963.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mehdi_Ben_Barka" title="Mehdi Ben Barka">Mehdi Ben Barka</a>, the leader of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Morocco" title="History of Morocco">Moroccan</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Union_of_Popular_Forces" title="National Union of Popular Forces">National Union of Popular Forces</a> (UNPF) and of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tricontinental_Conference" title="Tricontinental Conference">Tricontinental Conference</a>, which was supposed to prepare in 1966 in <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a> its first meeting gathering national liberation movements from all continents – related to the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>, but the Tricontinal Conference gathered liberation movements while the Non-Aligned were for the most part states – was "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forced_disappearance" title="Forced disappearance">disappeared</a>" in Paris in 1965, allegedly by Moroccan agents and French <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Police_officers" title="Police officers">police officers</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigerian</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Ahmadu_Bello" title="Ahmadu Bello">Ahmadu Bello</a> was assassinated in January 1966 during a coup which toppled Nigeria's post-independence government.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Mondlane" title="Eduardo Mondlane">Eduardo Mondlane</a>, the leader of <a href="/wiki/FRELIMO" title="FRELIMO">FRELIMO</a> and the father of <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambican</a> independence, was assassinated in 1969. Both the Portuguese intelligence or the Portuguese secret police PIDE/DGS and elements of FRELIMO, have been accused of killing Mondlane.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohamed_Bassiri" title="Mohamed Bassiri">Mohamed Bassiri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_people" title="Sahrawi people">Sahrawi</a> leader of the <a href="/wiki/Movement_for_the_Liberation_of_Saguia_el_Hamra_and_Wadi_el_Dhahab" title="Movement for the Liberation of Saguia el Hamra and Wadi el Dhahab">Movement for the Liberation of Saguia el Hamra and Wadi el Dhahab</a> was "disappeared" in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Aai%C3%BAn" title="El Aaiún">El Aaiún</a> in 1970, allegedly by the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Legion" title="Spanish Legion">Spanish Legion</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Am%C3%ADlcar_Cabral" title="Amílcar Cabral">Amílcar Cabral</a> was killed on January 20, 1973, by PAIGC rival Inocêncio Kani, with the help of Portuguese agents operating within the PAIGC.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_colonies">Current colonies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Current colonies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, under "Chapter XI: Declaration Regarding Non-Self Governing Territories" of the <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_the_United_Nations" title="Charter of the United Nations">Charter of the United Nations</a>, defines Non-Self Governing Nations (NSGSs) as "territories whose people have not yet attained a full measure of self-government"—the contemporary definition of <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonialism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> After the conclusion of World War II with the surrender of the Axis Powers in 1945, and two decades into the latter half of the 20th century, over three dozen "states in Asia and Africa achieved autonomy or outright independence" from European administering powers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> As of 2020, 17 territories remain under Chapter XI distinction:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-72">[72]</a></sup>
</p>

<td><a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a>

<td>1946–47, 1986

<td>1946–47, 2013
