<p>"On 26 February 1976, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> informed the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">Secretary-General</a> that as of that date it had terminated its presence in the Territory of the Sahara and deemed it necessary to place on record that Spain considered itself thenceforth exempt from any responsibility of any international nature in connection with the administration of the Territory, in view of the cessation of its participation in the temporary administration established for the Territory. In 1990, the General Assembly reaffirmed that the question of Western Sahara was a question of decolonization which remained to be completed by the people of Western Sahara."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-72">[72]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 10 December 2010, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> published its official <a href="/wiki/Decree" title="Decree">decree</a>, announcing the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Decade_for_the_Eradication_of_Colonialism" title="International Decade for the Eradication of Colonialism">Third International Decade for the Eradication of Colonialism</a></i> wherein the United Nations declared its "renewal of the call to States Members of the United Nations to speed up the process of decolonization towards the complete elimination of colonialism".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> According to an article by scholar John Quintero, "given the modern emphasis on the equality of states and inalienable nature of their sovereignty, many people do not realize that these non-self-governing structures still exist".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Some activists have claimed that the attention of the United Nations was "further diverted from the social and economic agenda [for decolonization] towards "firefighting and extinguishing” armed conflicts". Advocates have stressed that the United Nations "[remains] the last refuge of hope for peoples under the yolk <i>[sic]</i> of colonialism".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-75">[75]</a></sup> Furthermore, on 19 May 2015, <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">UN Secretary-General</a> <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> addressed the attendants of the Caribbean Regional Seminar on Decolonization, urging international political leaders to "build on [the success of precedent decolonization efforts and] towards fully eradicating colonialism by 2020".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-75">[75]</a></sup>
</p><p>The sovereignty of the <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Archipelago" title="Chagos Archipelago">Chagos Archipelago</a> in the Indian Ocean is <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Archipelago_sovereignty_dispute" title="Chagos Archipelago sovereignty dispute">disputed</a> between the United Kingdom and <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a>. In February 2019, the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a> ruled that the United Kingdom must transfer the islands to Mauritius as they were not legally separated from the latter in 1965.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> On 22 May 2019, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> debated and adopted a resolution that affirmed that the Chagos Archipelago "forms an integral part of the territory of Mauritius."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The UK does not recognize Mauritius' sovereignty claim over the Chagos Archipelago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> In October 2020, Mauritian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Pravind_Jugnauth" title="Pravind Jugnauth">Pravind Jugnauth</a> described the British and American governments as "hypocrites" and "champions of double talk" over their response to the dispute.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous_decolonization_theory">Indigenous decolonization theory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Indigenous decolonization theory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Indigenous_decolonization" title="Indigenous decolonization">Indigenous decolonization</a> theory views Western <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eurocentric" title="Eurocentric">Eurocentric</a> historical accounts and political discourse as an ongoing political construct that attempts to negate Indigenous peoples and their experiences around the world. Indigenous people of the world precede and negate all Eurocentric colonization projects and the resulting historical constructs, popular discourse, conceptualizations, and theory. In this view, the independence of European-styled former Western-European colonies, such as the United States, Australia, and Brazil, is conceptualized as ongoing neo-colonization projects of <a href="/wiki/Settler_colonialism" title="Settler colonialism">settler colonialism</a> and not as decolonization. The creation of these states merely continued ongoing European colonialism. Any former European colony not free of Western European influence fits such a concept. Examples of such former colonies include South Africa, Australia, Mexico, Brazil, and the USA. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Consequences_of_decolonization">Consequences of decolonization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Consequences of decolonization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A 2019 study found that "democracy levels increased sharply as colonies gained internal autonomy in the period immediately before their independence. However, conflict, revenue growth, and economic growth did not systematically differ before and after independence."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to political theorist Kevin Duong, decolonization "may have been the century’s greatest act of disenfranchisement", as numerous anti-colonial activists primarily pursued universal suffrage within empires rather than independence: "As dependent territories became nation-states, they lost their voice in metropolitan assemblies whose affairs affected them long after independence."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup>
</p><p>David Strange writes that the loss of their empires turned France and Britain into "second-rate powers."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Decolonising_global_health">Decolonising global health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Decolonising global health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Global health as a discipline is widely acknwoledged to be of imperial origin and the need for its decolonisation has been widely recognised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Dismantling the feudal structure of global health has been mentioned to be a key decolonisation agenda<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup>
</p>

Zed Books. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1848139534" title="Special:BookSources/978-1848139534"><bdi>978-1848139534</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Decolonizing+Methodologies%3A+Research+and+Indigenous+Peoples&amp;rft.pub=Zed+Books&amp;rft.date=2013&amp;rft.isbn=978-1848139534&amp;rft.aulast=Tuhiwai+Smith&amp;rft.aufirst=Linda&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ADecolonization"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://unu.edu/publications/articles/residual-colonialism-in-the-21st-century.html" rel="nofollow">"Residual Colonialism In The 21St Century"</a>. <i>United Nations University</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2019-10-18</span></span>. <q>The decolonization agenda championed by the United Nations is not based exclusively on independence. There are three other ways in which an NSGT can exercise self-determination and reach a full measure of self-government (all of them equally legitimate): integration within the administering power, free association with the administering power, or some other mutually agreed upon option for self-rule. [...] It is the exercise of the human right of self-determination, rather than independence per se, that the United Nations has continued to push for.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=United+Nations+University&amp;rft.atitle=Residual+Colonialism+In+The+21St+Century&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Funu.edu%2Fpublications%2Farticles%2Fresidual-colonialism-in-the-21st-century.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ADecolonization"></span></span>
</li>

<li>Strayer, Robert. “Decolonisation, Democratisation, and Communist Reform: The Soviet Collapse in Comparative Perspective,” Journal of World History 12#2 (2001), 375–406. <a class="external text" href="http://www.learner.org/courses/worldhistory/support/reading_26_3.pdf" rel="nofollow">online</a> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20150224051615/http://www.learner.org/courses/worldhistory/support/reading_26_3.pdf" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> 2015-02-24 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a></li>
<li>Thomas, Martin, Bob Moore, and Lawrence J. Butler. <i>Crises of Empire: Decolonisation and Europe's imperial states</i> (Bloomsbury Publishing, 2015)</li>
